After the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs received the content of Mr. Pittman's speech in the Senate on the 10th, they felt extremely unpleasant about his lack of knowledge of Japanese policy and his incomprehensible criticisms and slander. They are surprised to understand why such an important figure as the chairman of the US Senate Foreign Relations Committee made such remarks. According to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the words of the US Chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee are too ignorant, and the calm American people will not be greatly stimulated by such remarks. However, those in charge who bear heavy responsibilities have repeatedly seen in past examples what kind of adverse effects the publication of unnecessarily provocative and harsh voices has on diplomatic relations. Japan's policy towards East Asia aims to establish peace and is by no means to break the Open Door Principle or to monopolize East Asia by force. With this view, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will not make Mr. Pittman's speech a problem, but will treat it as a promotional speech for the presidential election. (11th, Allied News Agency dispatch)

Washington. Saito Hiroshi, the Japanese Ambassador to the United States, refused to comment after Pittman, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, delivered a speech in the Senate criticizing Japan's policy towards China, but said, "Japan has no intention of closing the door to China and excluding the commerce of the United States and other countries." It is absurd to talk about a war between Japan and the United States. There is no reason to change my view, and most people in the United States have the same feeling. (10th, Havas dispatch)

This is what the Soviet Russian government has long urged the great powers to pay attention to. Even the United Kingdom is well aware of the situation of Japanese imperialism threatening peace." The only thing left for all peace-loving countries in the world is to rise up and strive to organize a collective security system to deal with it. (11th, Havas dispatch)

This policy is completely different from what the Japanese are doing. In fact, China and the West have extremely important relations. It is not too late to help China now, but what is even more important than roads and railways is to enable farmers to return home and sell their products. (11th, Reuters dispatch)

Russian Newspaper Reveals Conspiracy: Japan and Germany Secretly Colluding 49

At the same time, the precedents created by the Kwantung Army on the Soviet border only lead to the ruthless destruction of the invading forces. Their provocations on the borders of the Soviet Union and the Mongolian People's Republic also serve the same purpose. They want to make the global situation extremely tense and create an environment on the border that is conducive to the future aggressive intentions of Japanese imperialism. *Pravda* further stated that newspapers around the world have reported on a Japanese-German military alliance, with Poland, Hungary, and Finland possibly joining. This is by no means a coincidence. For example, the Japanese-Manchukuo provocations and the issues raised by Germany in the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland coincide. At this moment, it is not difficult for us to discover the direct connection and mutual dependence between the two most belligerent, reactionary, and aggressive imperialist countries in the world. Their objectives are completely clear. Both Japan and Germany want to create a new imperialist bloc, strengthen their position, and at the same time threaten peaceful countries and undermine their cooperation through their provocative policies. This is why the recent situation is so worrying for all countries. Therefore, believers in peace must respond to the collective actions of aggressor countries with close collective action," (TASS dispatch, 11th).

League of Nations Oil Embargo Report to be Finalized in Geneva Soon; Sanctions Can Be Applied to Other Countries 53

Geneva.

The report to be submitted by the Committee of Experts on the issue of oil embargoes, appointed by the League of Nations' Committee of Eighteen, will be finalized in Geneva soon. According to well-informed sources, the Committee will make recommendations on the commercial and financial sanctions against aggressor countries stipulated in Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, and on various raw material embargo measures, so that they can be applied to the Italian-Ethiopian dispute and similar disputes in the future, (Havas dispatch, 11th).

Geneva.

The League of Nations' Committee of Eighteen originally intended to take the attitude adopted by the US Congress on this issue when voting on the new Neutrality Act as a guide to the issue of an oil embargo against Italy. The fact that the US Congress is about to extend the current Neutrality Act for another year is also irrelevant. Ethiopian Army Fights Bravely, Attempts to Recover Magal City; Italian Army Defends Firmly, Ultimately Failing; Ethiopian Progress on the Southern Front 55

Addis Ababa. Our correspondent Ochanat reports that, according to government officials here, the Ethiopian army on the southern front has occupied the Italian sentry camp in Gulati in the Ogaden region. The place is located southeast of Sassabaneh (the location of the Ethiopian army's forward headquarters), and many Italian soldiers have been killed, but the details are unknown, (Havas dispatch, 11th).

Addis Ababa. According to semi-official news received here, the Ethiopian army is making every effort to recover Magal. General Seyoum is leading the army to attack the Italian army fiercely, but because the Italian army's defensive works are extremely solid, including three barbed wire obstacles, each about six feet high, the Ethiopian army is repeatedly shot down by Italian machine guns despite their desperate advances. After a full day of fierce fighting, General Seyoum finally retreated due to excessive losses, (Reuters dispatch, 11th).

Dessie. Our special correspondent reports that at 9:20 AM on Sunday this week, several Italian military aircraft came here to drop bombs, for a total of two times. The first time, a bomb landed and exploded near St. Michael's Church, only 200 meters away from the royal palace. Then, several bombs fell around the former Italian consulate. Presumably, the Italian army suspected that the Ethiopian emperor's camp was located in the consulate, so they dropped the most bombs here, totaling more than a hundred. Two people were killed and five were injured, and three houses were burned down, (Havas dispatch, 10th).

Rome. According to well-informed Italian observers here, Italians may not gain much profit after Abyssinia is completely conquered. A certain Fascist Party member claimed that the war cost a lot. Even if we can occupy Abyssinia, we will be forced to hand it over to the bankers of the United Kingdom, the United States, and France. What we can obtain is only the sacrifice of lives and empty honor. Only they can enjoy the gold, (National Telegram, 10th).

Rome. According to the authorities, a total of 341 white soldiers died in Africa in January, four died from injuries, 92 died from illness, and three were missing. In the 13 months from January 1, 1935, to January 31, 1936, a total of 844 Italian white soldiers died, and the number of deaths in January of this year exceeded half of this number, which is enough to show the intensity of the Abyssinian war, (Reuters dispatch, 11th).

Qualitative Restrictions on Naval Issues: The United Kingdom, the United States, France, and Italy Have Approached an Agreement; Battleships Temporarily Set at 35,000 Tons; New Naval Treaty to Begin Drafting Immediately 56

London. On the issue of qualitative restrictions in the naval conference, the opinions of the four countries of the United Kingdom, France, Italy, and the United States have varied, and the stalemate has lasted for many days. Until today, after the representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and the United States held talks, the situation suddenly changed, and a compromise has been reached in fact. This afternoon, the group of experts under the General Committee continued to meet to discuss the issue of battleship tonnage. It is reported that the French representative has agreed to temporarily stipulate the maximum limit of battleship tonnage at 35,000 tons. Therefore, the United Kingdom and the United States can prepare to build ships in accordance with their original proposals. However, in the draft naval treaty, the two countries must recognize that the ultimate goal should be to stipulate 27,000 tons as the maximum limit in the shortest possible time. The reason why the situation suddenly changed today is that the United Kingdom indicated that it could make concessions politically on the issue of inviting Germany to join the four-nation conference. Therefore, France no longer insisted on its original proposal of 27,000 tons or 28,000 tons, and made concessions to the United Kingdom on the issue of qualitative restrictions in exchange. It is reported that the United Kingdom has now agreed to first order a four-nation naval agreement, and then submit it to all other naval nations. It is also reported that the French Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Corbin, visited the US Chief Representative Davis this morning and immediately stated to him that the purpose of convening the naval conference was to limit armaments, so the current limit of 35,000 tons for battleships should not be regarded as an immutable method. Since a compromise has been reached on the issue of battleship tonnage, the group of experts assigned a drafting committee to draft an agreement specifically for the qualitative restrictions of other types of ships. Its content must be based on the following outlines proposed by the United Kingdom:

Class A cruisers: 10,000 tons displacement, equipped with 6-inch or 8-inch guns.

Class B cruisers: 7,500 tons displacement, equipped with 6-inch guns.

Destroyers and light cruisers are merged into one category without establishing separate categories. However, theoretically, their displacement should not exceed 1,850 tons.

Submarines: 2,000 tons displacement, equipped with 5-inch guns.

Aircraft carriers: 22,000 tons displacement, equipped with 6-inch guns.

In addition, all ancillary issues, such as Article 14 of the Washington Naval Treaty, regarding the installation of weapons on all non-commercial vessels, and Articles 15, 16, 17, and 18, regarding the construction of warships by contracting states on behalf of non-contracting states, are all to be studied jointly by the drafting committee. As for shallow-water coastal defense cruisers, they are not subject to qualitative restrictions, but should also be notified before construction, (Havas dispatch, 10th).

London. After continued discussions at the naval conference today, it has reached the stage where treaty drafting can begin soon. The term will be approximately five or six years. The treaty will contain the points that have been agreed upon. The technical committee made rapid progress this afternoon and approved all of British Naval Minister Monsell's proposals except for the maximum type of warship. In the next few days, informal bilateral talks will be held to reach a compromise on the 35,000 tons proposed by the United States and the 27,500 tons proposed by France. The committee is scheduled to continue its meeting on Thursday, at which time it can begin the drafting of the treaty. According to Monsell's proposal: Battleships are limited to 35,000 tons, with 14-inch gun positions. There is a possibility of reducing this tonnage by 2,000 to 3,000 tons in the future. Aircraft carriers are limited to 22,000 tons, with 6-inch gun positions. This is intended to eliminate the difficulties caused by countries that have not signed the London Naval Treaty and have already engaged in building warships of the destroyer class. Submarines are limited to 2,000 tons, with 5-inch gun positions, (Reuters dispatch, 1st).

London. Regarding the qualitative restrictions issue of the naval conference, it was reported yesterday that the four countries of the United Kingdom, France, Italy, and the United States had reached an agreement in fact. It has been learned that this statement is not entirely accurate. The French delegation visited the British delegation again this morning and still insisted on 27,000 tons as the maximum tonnage for battleships. According to our correspondent, the French government has instructed its delegation to demand that the tonnage of battleships be reduced to below 35,000 tons, but this instruction is not definitive. If the four countries of the United Kingdom, France, Italy, and the United States cannot reach an agreement on this basis, then France still has room to change its position. In short, although there was progress in the negotiations between the representatives of the countries concerned yesterday, it would be premature to say that a formal agreement has been reached. What can be said is that the proposals previously put forward by France and Italy, namely insisting that the tonnage of battleships should be limited to 27,000 tons, may be conceded in order to facilitate the progress of the talks, that's all, (Havas dispatch, 11th).

French and Czech Foreign Ministers Discuss Central European Issues; Aimed at Promoting Cooperation Among Danube Countries 57

Paris. Czech Prime Minister Hodza visited Foreign Minister Flandin at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 4:30 PM today to discuss the issue of organizing Central European countries, until he took his leave at 5:15 PM. It is reported that the main goal of the two men's talks was to promote economic and political cooperation among Austria, Hungary, and the Little Entente countries (Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia), so as to get closer to each other. This organization will integrate the Rome Agreement signed by Italy, Austria, and Hungary in March of the previous year and the current Little Entente Pact into a Danube River system. In the future, if Germany wants to join, it will not be hindered. It is generally expected that since the Italian-Ethiopian dispute has not yet been resolved, a general agreement on the establishment of this organization may not be easy to achieve. Hodza told reporters after leaving the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, "My opinions and those of Mr. Flandin are completely consistent, and there are no differences even in trivial details." Tomorrow, the House of Representatives will discuss the ratification of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. Foreign Minister Flandin must attend the House of Representatives and has no time to meet foreign guests. Therefore, Hodza is scheduled to visit the Foreign Minister again the day after tomorrow to continue negotiations on Central European issues, (Havas dispatch, 10th).

Markets in places like Alipo have also closed their doors and suspended business again, (Reuters dispatch, 11th).

Jerusalem. After three weeks of boiling disputes, bloodshed, general strikes, etc., the domestic economic situation has stagnated, but these disputes are still increasing. The anti-French wave in all of Syria is becoming increasingly dangerous, and the declaration of martial law is imminent. The Speaker of the Syrian Parliament today sent a cable to the League of Nations and the French Foreign Ministry, protesting against the authorities' oppressive measures in Kuns and Hama, which led to bloody incidents. Fifty members of the Iraqi Parliament jointly sent a protest letter to the League of Nations' mandatory power, saying that French policy is to blame for all the disputes in Syria now. This situation is causing great concern in the United Kingdom, because this kind of indigenous people's national movement is strongly sympathized with by the Arabs in Palestine and Transjordan. German Unemployment Statistics; The Increase Last Month Was Very Small 63

Berlin. According to official statistics, the number of registered unemployed in Germany increased by 12,000 in January, compared to an increase of 524,000 in December last year. As of the end of January, the total increase was 2,520,000. The number of these unemployed who received government relief funds increased by 127,000 in January, and the number who did not receive relief funds decreased by 112,000. Judging from the above total number, the increase in the number of unemployed in January was very small, but the number of workers laid off by various factories was very large, so that the number of people receiving government relief funds actually increased, (Havas dispatch, 11th).

The President announced the reason for the cancellation of the three cases, saying that the Supreme Court recently ruled the Agricultural Adjustment Act invalid, which caused the two laws to lose their basis for existence, (National Telegram, 10th).

A Comparison of the Naval Strength of Five Countries 89

—Ang Ruo

Japan has withdrawn from the London Naval Conference, while the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and Italy have reached a compromise. However, the naval issue has become deeply entrenched, and even if these negotiations are successful, they will not have much significance. As for Japan, although it has left, its naval policy cannot be unaffected by the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries, as the positions of various naval powers are like a chain, not allowing individual actions. Here is a comparison of the naval strength of the United Kingdom, the United States, Japan, France, and Italy as of the end of last year:

(1) Capital Ships (Battleships and Battlecruisers)

The United Kingdom currently has fifteen ships, of which three are outdated, eight will reach their service limit this year, and another one will reach its service limit next year. (According to the 1930 London Naval Treaty, the service age of battleships is 20 years.) The remaining three ships were built in 1920 and 1927.

The United States currently has fifteen ships, of which three are outdated, four will reach their service limit this year, and another one will reach its service limit next year. The remaining seven ships were built between 1918 and 1923, so the newest one is already twelve years old.

Japan currently has nine ships, of which four are outdated, two will reach their service limit next year, and the remaining three were built between 1918 and 1921, so the newest one is already fourteen years old.

The above three countries are not currently building new battleships, nor do they have any plans to do so.

France currently has nine ships, of which seven are outdated, and two will reach their service limit this year. There are three ships under construction and one ship planned for construction (two ships of 26,500 tons and two ships of 35,000 tons).

Italy currently has four ships, of which three are outdated. The remaining two ships are so-called "pocket battleships," each with 10,000 tons according to the restrictions of the Treaty of Versailles. There are three ships under construction, of which two are 26,000 tons each, and the third pocket battleship is 10,000 tons.

(2) Cruisers

The United Kingdom currently has fifty-four ships, of which twenty-two are outdated (the age of cruisers is 16 years, but according to the London Treaty, those built after the end of 1919 have a service age of 20 years). There are nine ships under construction and three ships planned for construction, of which two have been tendered for construction. In terms of tonnage, there are seventeen ships between 9,000 and 10,000 tons, two ships between 8,000 and 9,000 tons, seven ships of 7,000 tons, and the rest are smaller.

The United States currently has twenty-six ships, of which one is outdated. There are fifteen ships between 9,000 and 10,000 tons, eleven ships of 7,000 tons, and twelve ships under construction, all to supplement the 10,000-ton cruisers (of which two have not yet been started).

Japan currently has forty ships, of which eleven are outdated (five are already 35 years old). There are three ships under construction and one ship planned for construction. As for their tonnage, there are twelve ships between 9,000 and 10,000 tons, two ships between 8,000 and 9,000 tons, and five ships of around 7,000 tons. The four ships under construction and planned for construction are each 8,500 tons.

France currently has seventeen ships, of which four are outdated. There are five ships under construction, each of 7,600 tons. The seven ships that have been completed are each 10,000 tons. There are four ships between 7,000 and 8,000 tons, and another old ship of 11,000 tons. In addition, France has thirty shallow-water gunboats between 2,000 and 2,600 tons. (According to the London Treaty, these shallow-water gunboats are also classified as cruisers, but France has not ratified this treaty.) There are two ships under construction, each of 2,884 tons.

Italy currently has twenty-seven ships, of which eleven are outdated. There are three ships under construction between 7,000 and 8,000 tons. Among the ships that have been completed, there are seven ships of 10,000 tons, one ship between 8,000 and 9,000 tons, and eight ships between 5,000 and 6,000 tons.

Germany currently has six ships, each of 6,000 tons (one of 5,400 tons). There are two ships under construction, both of 10,000 tons.

The United Kingdom currently has eight ships, of which one is outdated. There are four ships of around 22,000 tons and one ship under construction with the same tonnage.

The United States currently has four ships, of which one is outdated. There are two ships of 33,000 tons and three ships under construction, of which two are around 20,000 tons each.

Japan currently has six ships, of which one is outdated. There are two ships of 26,900 tons, and two ships each of 14,000 tons and 17,000 tons. There are two ships under construction and one ship planned for construction.

France and Italy have no aircraft carriers that have not reached their service limit, but according to the London Treaty, France has one 10,000-ton aircraft carrier.

(3) Submarines

The United Kingdom currently has fifty-one ships, of which fourteen are outdated. (According to the London Treaty, the age of submarines is 13 years.) There are nine ships under construction.

The United States currently has eighty-four ships, of which forty-five are outdated. There are sixteen ships under construction.

Japan currently has fifty-seven ships, of which eleven are outdated. There are ten ships under construction.

France currently has eighty-two ships (including eight mine-laying submarines), of which nine are outdated. There are eight ships under construction and two ships planned for construction.

Italy currently has sixty-four ships, of which eleven are outdated. There are thirteen ships under construction.

He Jian's Report on the Pursuit and Suppression of He Xiao's Bandits 90

And the Situation of the Reorganization Teams

Changsha Correspondence: He Jian, the Commander-in-Chief of the First Route Army for Bandit Suppression, has returned to the province from Changde, where he was supervising the suppression. On the 3rd, he attended an enlarged memorial week and reported on the general situation of pursuing and suppressing He Xiao's bandit gang, as well as the reorganization teams and the completion of the pacification work. The following is a record of his report:

"Today, I will give a brief report on the recent pursuit and suppression of He Xiao's bandit gang, as well as the situation in Hunan regarding pacification and the reorganization of the teams. After He Xiao's bandit gang sneaked out from Dayong Tankou, they wreaked havoc in many places. Although the National Army pursued them urgently, the only places where there was formal contact with the bandits were Chenxi, Xupu, Longtan Siwuchang, and Bianshui Bozhou in Huangxian. The most severely damaged bandit unit was the one in the Battle of Bianshui Bozhou, which suffered thousands of casualties. The second was the Battle of Wuwuchang, which also resulted in many casualties. In total, He Xiao's two bandits originally had more than 20,000 men. After the above-mentioned decisive battles, it is estimated that no more than 10,000 armed soldiers have fled into Guizhou. On the surface, it seems that they intend to flee north of the Wujiang River. However, the Red Bandits have always been opportunistic and fled in disarray, so it is not easy to judge their true intentions. However, a month ago, the bandits had fled to the Houchang area east of Wengan. Our General Commander Liu has led 3,000 troops into Guizhou to pursue and suppress them. It is estimated that Li's detachment passed through Kaijin Longgaogou Line on the 25th to pursue and suppress Yuqing. Fan's detachment advanced from Yinjiang to Tangtou. Guo Runian's troops advanced from Minjiachang to Shiqian. Although the Red Bandits have suffered heavy losses, our pursuing troops also face many difficulties. The bandits' movements average more than 100 li per day. Our troops can barely travel 100 li, so their movements are relatively slow. The reasons for this are as follows: In terms of action, the bandits are fleeing for their lives, so their movements are faster. In terms of supplies, whenever the bandits pass through a better place, they take what they need from the homes of so-called local tyrants and evil gentry. The National Army faces great difficulties in transporting supplies. In barren areas, the bandits have looted all the food, and the pursuing troops are even more short of food. In terms of climate, the weather is severely cold, with icy and frozen ground, making transportation extremely difficult. It is not easy to transport clothing and other supplies from the rear. The bandits take advantage of this opportunity to escape more easily. Due to these difficulties, they could not be eliminated within Hunan. Now that the bandits have fled far into Guizhou, there are even more difficulties. In the past, bandit suppression operations always had supply stations to provide everything. Now, the weather is bad and there are no supply stations. All the military supplies are handled by the troops themselves. Fortunately, the morale is extremely high. Whenever the troops encounter bandits, they bravely take the lead and inflict heavy losses on them. Now that winter is over and spring is coming, and the weather is warm, as long as the bandits do not flee elsewhere, I believe that they still have the possibility of being eliminated in this encirclement. Now that He Xiao's bandit gang has fled far into Guizhou, the remaining bandits in western Hunan still include a part of the pseudo-18th Division. In other counties, there are only dozens or hundreds of scattered bandits with guns, who still need to be cleared. We are now requesting instructions from the headquarters, intending to take advantage of this opportunity to transfer a part of the troops to cooperate with the local teams to clear and suppress the bandits in different areas, and strive to complete the pacification work in Hunan in the shortest possible time and consolidate the security of the entire province. However, one thing that deserves our attention the most and should be thoroughly understood is the issue of security teams. The security teams are very important to the security of the whole province, and also has great significance for national defense. Some Hunan compatriots who are concerned about Hunan affairs have made remarks about the Hunan teams that are absolutely contrary to the facts. I have repeatedly explained this in Nanjing. Unexpectedly, recently, there are still people who say that the Hunan teams are useless and request to return the team guns for the people to defend themselves. This matter is related to the security of the entire province and cannot be ignored. Therefore, I will not hesitate to repeat a simple report. The Hunan teams were originally the former local militias. Although they have been reorganized for several years, they have not yet reached the planned goals. Therefore, it cannot be said how good they are. However, if they are dogmatically said to be truly useless, then I dare say that this is indeed a statement that violates the facts. Moreover, the achievements of the Hunan teams are indeed above those of any other province. This can be proven by facts. Before the reorganization, each county in Hunan had local militias. Most of them had one or two thousand guns, and at least six or seven hundred guns. The salaries and expenses were generally apportioned locally, and the government could not intervene. Although the numbers were unknown, it is estimated that they were not small. However, what was the situation of bandit suppression at that time? Everyone knows. Bandit robberies often occurred in Yue Li Mountain across the river. The people in Baoqing could not even leave the city. The situation in Pingliu was even worse. In other counties, banditry was often heard. After the reorganization, the first step was to unify the county. The teams in Village A and Village B, which could not take care of each other in the past, could be mobilized at any time to help each other. In the past, team guns were occupied by a few wealthy gentry as their personal property. Now, they can be used as the common property of the people of the whole county and planned as a whole. As for the team expenses, the extremely inconsistent and unfair apportionment methods of the past have been abolished, and a team tax surcharge with equal burden has been established. These are all facts that the 20 million people of Hunan have seen and heard. The former Security Command assigned the teams to different areas to be responsible for the suppression. Scattered bandits in various places have been gradually eliminated, and the local areas have been roughly stabilized. It cannot be said that this is only the power of the teams. After the unification of the province, the teams have made the greatest contribution, which is not known to the outside world and deserves to be stated. There are three things: When the Fourth Route Army left the province to assist in the suppression of the Red Bandits in Jiangxi and Hubei, only the 19th Division was left in Hunan. The area was vast and the troops were few. How could they be deployed? The security of various places in Hunan was entirely maintained with the assistance of the teams. When the National Army was engaged in a large-scale bandit suppression in Jiangxi, more than a dozen Hunan Provincial teams were transferred to areas outside the province in the border areas of Hubei and Jiangxi to be responsible for blocking the bandits, so the degree of preservation can be imagined. This point cannot be achieved by the teams of any province. When Zhu Mao's large force emerged from their nests and fled through Hunan to Sichuan, most of the Fourth Route Army had already left the province to suppress the bandits. In southern Hunan, all the troops were only one or two divisions. The disparity in numbers was great, and the situation was urgent. At that time, teams from all over the place were mobilized to guard the blockhouses and intercept them along the way, so that Zhu Mao's bandit crowd of more than 100,000 did not dare to stay in southern Hunan. This was really the assistance of the teams. Not only can the teams from other provinces not do this, but even the formal army cannot easily take on this heavy task. The teams in Guangxi have always been praised by the whole country, and the personnel sent by Guangxi to Hunan for inspection have seen that the mobilization of Hunan teams is more flexible than that of Guangxi after they looked at the Hunan teams. Some people attributed the bandit suppression in western Hunan, regarding the battle in the Lishui River Basin, to the teams. However, it is not the responsibility of the Hunan teams, and the teams have worked very hard. Because the two decisive battles to recover the lost land occupied by the bandits in the Lishui River Basin were fought by our 19th Division and various teams. When He Xiao's bandit gang fled to Anhua and Xinhua, I was still in the capital. Many people said that the teams were useless and could not suppress the bandits. After I returned to Hunan, I investigated in detail and confirmed that it was not the relationship of the teams, but the lack of effort of one or two people leading the teams. According to a certain regimental adjutant of Xu's department who escaped from the bandits and was captured, the teams along the way often only had dozens of guns, and they came out to fight with the bandits, greatly hindering the bandits' actions. Therefore, the bandits hated the teams very much. Moreover, He Xiao's bandit gang had one or two thousand men. It is not easy for the formal army to send one or two divisions to suppress them. How can the few teams be held responsible for eliminating the bandit gang? Some people also say that when the teams are transferred away from their own counties, if bandits come, there are no teams in the area and there is no way to resist. Therefore, they request the return of the team guns for self-defense. After the unified command and dispatch of the teams, the distribution of the teams is determined based on the local situation. If the bandits take advantage of the emptiness to harass the area, it is true that the area may feel empty due to the reason that the troops were not able to be transferred in time. However, if the team guns in each county are left to each county for self-defense, and cannot be under the unified command and dispatch of the security office, not to mention the coming of large bandit gangs, they cannot be dealt with by the team guns left for self-defense in the county. The teams in other counties cannot take care of each other because they are left for local self-defense. The result will surely revert to the situation before the reorganization, and the country will be full of bandits. Therefore, in the current distribution of the teams, some places are not stationed, but there are also teams that are less than one regiment, but are stationed in two or three regiments or more. This is the reason for considering the local security situation and coordinating the dispatch. Moreover, local security has a very important relationship with neighboring areas. Sometimes, stationing in neighboring counties to suppress bandits is to directly consolidate the security of the county and prevent bandits from invading the county. I hope that all people in the province will have a thorough understanding of this point. In short, the teams in Hunan cannot be said to be good because they have not yet reached the intended purpose of reorganization. However, compared with before the reorganization, there is indeed a world of difference. In particular, the item of team salaries has reduced the burden on the people a lot. In the era of the former local militia system, there were countless donations and expenses. After unification with the county, the number was more than 10 million. When it was unified with the province, it initially required more than 8 million yuan per year, and the third district in western Hunan was not included. Later, based on the view of emphasizing quality rather than quantity, it was repeatedly downsized, and now it only needs more than 4 million yuan per year, which is a reduction of more than 3 million yuan per year. In addition, the reduction and exemption of all exorbitant taxes related to team taxes are not included. In addition, there are also doubts about the item of arrears of team salaries. The security office has been instructed to prepare a detailed statement of income and expenditure, which will be published in the newspaper soon, so that all gentry in the province can thoroughly understand the actual situation. The arrears of team salaries are probably only several hundred thousand yuan. However, the additional team taxes accumulated in the people but not yet collected, excluding those that have been exempted, are still more than 3 million yuan. Therefore, the reason for the arrears of team salaries is actually due to the failure to collect additional team taxes. It is not that the management personnel have any problems. Moreover, a fund management and supervision committee has been set up to supervise and report on a monthly basis. As for some people who advocate that each county should have a team of one regiment or one battalion stationed, this is not only not possible in practice, but also the handling of the teams is entirely in accordance with the security system issued by the headquarters. Hunan Province cannot be unique. The progress of the Hunan teams is relatively ahead of other provinces. Therefore, in recent years, many provinces have requisitioned materials from Hunan Province for reference. If we must say that team guns will not be returned to each county, and the people cannot defend themselves, and the bandits cannot be eliminated, regardless of the intention, it is actually contrary to the facts. Now, the Military Affairs Committee has sent personnel to Hunan to check the teams. The inspection committee will have a clear report on what the Hunan teams are like in the future, so I will not say much. Now that He Xiao's bandit gang has fled far away, we must take advantage of this opportunity to complete the pacification work in the entire province of Hunan in the shortest possible time. I hope that all people in the province will rise up and help together, so that we can thoroughly eliminate the scattered bandits in various places in the territory. The chairman of the committee attaches great importance to Hunan and has great expectations. When he summoned students from various places for training this time, he made it very clear about his determination and methods for the future of the country. All of us in Hunan must follow the will of the chairman of the committee and move forward together, so as to shoulder the mission of saving the country and live up to the expectations of all parties. Let us all work together!"

Prohibition of Opium Cultivation in Gansu Province in Progress 91

Provincial Government Orders Strict Prohibition of Cultivation in All Counties

Lanzhou Correspondence: The funds for the Gansu Provincial Opium Prohibition Committee and the Opium Prohibition Bureau were previously instructed by the Chairman's Headquarters to be reduced appropriately. The provincial government immediately submitted the organizational regulations of the Opium Prohibition Committee to the headquarters for record. It has now been ordered to change the establishment of one section chief and four to eight section members for each section to one section chief and two to four section members for each section. After receiving the order, the provincial government believed that the matter of the Opium Prohibition Bureau was the same, and it was not appropriate to be unique, so it should also be reduced appropriately to save public funds. It was resolved at the 378th provincial affairs meeting: The funds for the Opium Prohibition Committee were reduced by one-third. The drug rehabilitation center was abolished, and all drug rehabilitation matters were entrusted to the provincial hospital. The registration office for opium addicts was abolished, and all registration matters were entrusted to Gaolan County. The funds for the Opium Prohibition Bureau were reduced by one-third. The funds for the Accountant Specialist's Office were reduced by one-third. The funds for the Supervision Office were reduced by one-third. Separate letters have been sent to the two agencies to prepare separate budgets, and they will be implemented from February 16. It is estimated that more than 50,000 yuan can be saved each year.

Chairman Yu of the provincial government, in order to thoroughly prohibit opium cultivation, especially issued a notice and order to the 32 counties and bureaus that had already prohibited opium cultivation, ordering them to strictly investigate and prohibit it. He also ordered the county magistrates to personally conduct on-site inspections in various villages and towns to ensure that no stems and plants were found or that opium was secretly cultivated again. It is reported that the notice has been issued, and it roughly stated: "It has been decided that opium cultivation will be prohibited in stages, and the government is determined and cannot change this. Anyone who has already planted opium must plow it up as soon as possible and replant it with crops. Those who have not planted opium must not sow opium seeds again. Be careful not to wait and see or try to experiment. After the notice is issued, if anyone dares to plant opium secretly, once discovered, the land will be confiscated in full and the person will be punished by law. There will be no leniency."

The Largest Resource in the Northeast: The Distribution of Coal Mines 92

Publication by the South Manchuria Railway Geological Survey Hall: The Reserve is 4.8 Billion Tons

Shenyang Correspondence: Regarding the coalfields in the Northeast, according to the South Manchuria Railway Geological Survey Hall, the entire Northeast is divided into two regions, namely, the area between Tieling in "Fengtian Province" and Chengde in Rehe in the west, and Huning in "Jiandao Province" in the east, forming a straight line from the northeast to the southwest. The southern part is the Paleozoic rock layer, and the northern part is the Mesozoic rock layer. In the southern Paleozoic rock layer, there are two layers of stone coal seams. The main coalfield locations are the southeastern area of Chengde in Rehe, the area near Jinzhou in Jinzhou Province, the area east of Benxi Lake in "Fengtian Province", the southern part of Hailong in "Fengtian Province", the area near Songgang, and the Wuhu Mouth of the Far East Peninsula. In the northern Mesozoic rock layer, there is the Zhujiang stone coal seam. The main coalfield locations are the southern area of Fujin in "Sanjiang Province", the area near Heligang Linkou, the area near Mishan Lishu Bo in "Binjiang Province", the area near Jiaohe Gangyao Huoshizhen in "Jilin Province", Zhalainuoer in "Xinganbei Province", the area near Beipiao in "Jinzhou Province", the area west of Fuxin in "Rehe Province", and its vicinity. Within the southern region, there are still the Fushun coalfield in "Fengtian Province" and the Hunchun coalfield in "Jiandao Province" in the Cenozoic Tertiary period. Observing the overall distribution, the entire Northeast is divided into two parts for investigation, namely, from Chifeng in "Rehe Province" through the south of Harbin, to Luobei in "Sanjiang Province", roughly dividing the Northeast along a line from the northwest to the south. It is found that there are extremely many coalfields in the southeast, and the distribution in the west is quite sparse. Those in the northwest are mostly lignite. However, the northwest has a sparse population and is a dense forest rarely visited by people, or a vast grassland, with very few exposed strata, and there are few opportunities to discover coalfields. As for the estimation of coal reserves, it is estimated to be 4.8 billion tons. The following is a list of the output of each place (unit: ton). As for those with reserves of more than 100 million tons, they are as follows:

Although there are only eight coalfields mentioned above, according to recent surveys, those imagined to be over 100 million tons still include Hunchun in "Jiandao Province". In addition to the previously well-known Xinqiu in the Fuxin coalfield, the original layer has been discovered near Sunjiawan, and the increase in imagined reserves is quite significant.

Kunshan: Recent Interrogation of the Embezzlement Case of the Former Director of the Construction Bureau 94

Wu Junyu, the former director of the Construction Bureau of this county, was accused of embezzling public funds when recruiting laborers during the January 28th Shanghai War. He was reported to the former county party department by Yi Ren, a county resident. Zhu Jingzhi, a member of the Supervisory Committee, conducted a serious investigation and found that the embezzlement was true. Cheng Ruji, the former county magistrate, also found that Wu had embezzled more than 17,000 yuan of public funds. He was immediately arrested and sent to the province. The following year, he was transferred to the court for interrogation and sentenced to three years and six months in prison. When the term expired in November last year, he was sent back to the original county to recover the embezzled funds. Immediately, people from all walks of life and local gentry petitioned the county government to submit a report to the province, requesting strict pursuit to warn against corruption. The judiciary also conducted a trial, but Wu refused to repay the funds, claiming that he was unable to do so. Recently, it was heard that he will apply to seal up his property and auction it off to repay the debt.

Wuxi: Strange Bird with Two Heads and Wooden Tag on its Foot 95

At 8:50 AM yesterday, a gray strange bird resembling an eagle suddenly fell from the sky onto the roof of Taihetang Pharmacy in Shuangbanqiao, the eighth district of this county. It weighed three to five kilograms. It was spotted by a passerby who informed the store and asked them to catch the bird. It was found that there was a small wooden tag on its foot with the words "Changshou Xiangji" branded on it, the meaning of which was unknown. It is now being raised in the store. In addition, near Baojiazhuang in Nanfangquan Town, the third district, a strange bird suddenly flew from the air the day before yesterday. It was as fat as a hen, with a ferocious appearance. It soared in the sky, sometimes swooping down to catch chickens, and sometimes chasing crows and magpies. Birds in the nearby airspace have disappeared. Later, the villagers caught it with a net. There was a copper bell tied to its tail feathers, and a copper tag with the words "Sushiqiao" engraved on it. No one knows this kind of strange bird, which is very bizarre. It is also heard that a strange homing pigeon was also found in Changshu County a few days ago.

Changzhou: Reorganization of the Fire Brigade and Fire Donation 96

The Wuyi Fire Brigade Union previously felt that the 20% fire donation from various towns was decreasing, making it difficult to handle the fire service in various districts. The monthly electricity bill is very high, so it is planned to convene another meeting to request the electricity plant to reduce the fee by half, or follow the example of the Shanghai water and electricity plant merger method and have the electricity plant take over the operation.

Many New Opium Addicts Registered 98

The new opium addicts registration in this province started in January. In order to prevent the addicts from evading, a method of searching door-to-door was ordered. The Baojia chiefs and the Public Security Bureau would search door-to-door. The effect has been very significant in January. There are now more than 60,000 new opium addicts in the province, with Jiangdu, Changshu, Songjiang, Taicang, Zhenjiang, and Nantong accounting for the most. With the half-month deadline approaching, many wealthy households and giants in various places are still waiting and seeing and evading. A telegram has been sent again to various counties to break through the face and conduct a serious search, forcing registration. Those who have several people in one family smoking opium and only have one license are also strictly prohibited, so as to ensure that no one is missed and the six-year prohibition plan is completed.

Funing: Robbing a Widow Leads to Disaster 101

In Wangji Township, Benyi, Zhuang Xingyang had a widow named Mei Yiniang. On the 8th, a matchmaker arranged for her to marry Yang Zhenwang of the same village. The betrothal gift had been handed over by the matchmaker. Unexpectedly, Yang Zhenhang, who had also coveted her for a long time, led many people on the night of the 9th and forcibly robbed Mei Yiniang. Yang Zhenwang was unwilling and reported Yang Zhenhang's robbery of the widow to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau. Liang Baoyu, the chief of the police station, and police officer Chen Weigong, etc., were dispatched to investigate. The villagers in the township saw the police and beat gongs to gather a crowd, surrounding the police and robbing the box guns and handguns they carried. During the fight for the guns, the trigger was accidentally pulled, and the bullet was fired, injuring Yang Yaoqing and Tian Xiao Erzi. The order was in chaos for a while, and the people then tied up police officer Liang and others, together with the injured, and sent them to the county government. On the 10th, Shan Gao, the presiding judge, held a court hearing to investigate the incident, and ordered the injured to be sent to Dasheng Hospital for treatment. Police officer Liang and others were handed over to Inspector Huang of the bureau to take them back. Yang Pufu and Yang Yuqing, who gathered a crowd to commit the crime, were handed over to the police for custody and awaiting investigation.

Hangzhou: Agricultural Extension Funding Secured 102

In order to improve agriculture and increase production, the Zhejiang Construction Department has designated Hangzhou City and County, Haining, Yiwu, Yuhang, Tongxiang, Lin'an, Yuqian, Wuxing, Deqing, Zhenhai, Jiaxing, and Cixi as rice and wheat extension areas. Hangzhou County, Zhenhai, Cixi, Yin County, Dinghai, Xiaoshan, Yuyao, Shangyu, Haiyan are designated as cotton extension areas. A large number of improved cotton and rice varieties will be promoted, covering a total of 300,000 mu. The funding required is 100,000 yuan, which is quite difficult to raise. Therefore, agricultural funding has been secured. A meeting will be held in the province on the 17th of this month to discuss the extension policy, and the county magistrates of various districts will come to the province to attend.

Ningbo: Implementation of Licensed Prostitution in Yong Port 105

Licensed prostitution was strictly prohibited in this port city upon the establishment of the municipal government in 1927. Now, nine years later, due to the proliferation of clandestine prostitution and the decline of government-licensed prostitution, the income from prostitution taxes has dwindled. Consequently, the political and police authorities have jointly decided to legalize public prostitution. Regulations for its control have been submitted to the provincial government for approval and promulgation. Once "Brothel Permits," "Brothel Licenses," and "Prostitutes' Business Licenses" are printed, the plan can be implemented. Future revenue from prostitution taxes will supplement local political and police expenditures.

Fire on Houtang Road Injures More Than Ten 106

A fire broke out at 3:10 AM on the 9th at Yongfengtai Southern Goods Store, No. 56 Houtang Road, Jiangdong, in this city. The fire, caused by the burning of a cake bed by the drying oven, resulted in a complete conflagration. In addition to the total destruction of the three-story building of the store, two two-story buildings, and one building of the Yuantai Rice Store, as well as the three-story building of the Xinhongtai Pickled Goods Store, seven employees of the store, including Shen Xinfa, Xu Yande, Xuan Binquan, Tang Pinshan, Hu Heting, Xiang Sanmei, and Qiu Xinglai, suffered serious injuries after jumping from windows in a hurried escape. Five other employees, including Chai Mingshui, Xu Zhizhen, Zhou Xingfu, Shen Jiarui, and Xiang Simei, sustained minor injuries after descending via ropes. Furthermore, Xu Zhang, the wife of the owner of Yuantai Rice Store, and her niece, Zhu Qian, were also seriously injured after jumping from a window.

Shaoxing: Money Exchange Industry Agrees on Operating Policies 107

Due to the economic downturn, the Shaoxing money exchange industry, in addition to tightening lending, specifically decided on operating policies for the year 1936 yesterday. The main points include: All receipts and remittances will be based on checks; business hours will be from 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM daily, but may be extended during holidays or when necessary; fixed-term loans will continue to be divided into two periods, the end of April and the end of October; the daily lending rate will be publicly announced at one percent starting April 6, and from May 1, the highest rate will be limited to five percent until fifteen days before the end of the year; the term for buying and selling Shanghai remittances is four days, with a handling fee of five cents per hundred yuan; the term for Ningbo-Hangzhou remittances is three days, with a handling fee of two and a half cents per hundred yuan; for currency exchange, a handling fee of five cents per hundred yuan will be charged for receiving legal tender, and a handling fee of two cents per hundred yuan will be charged for disbursing legal tender. Transactions involving silver and copper subsidiary coins will be handled in accordance with the regulations set by the ministry.

Saving lives is as critical as saving a life. Donate an extra cent to save an extra life.

Letter: Letter from Landis & Company 108

To the Editor,

Having read the article in the foreign news section on the third page of your newspaper on February 6 concerning the American merchant claiming damages for inferior silk, which stated that last year's European sales of Chinese silk were active and the market improved, so that the silk mills in both Shanghai and Wuxi had made considerable profits. However, some speculative silk mills specialize in crude manufacturing, seeking only rapid production without regard for overseas credit, resulting in poor quality products. Now, various American silk factories and hosiery factories have suffered significant losses due to purchasing this Chinese silk. A special letter was sent to Landis & Company, an American merchant in Shanghai managing Chinese silk exports, claiming damages of US$87,000, equivalent to approximately 260,000 Chinese yuan. After receiving the letter, the company turned to the silk mill associations in Shanghai and Wuxi to negotiate compensation. We are extremely astonished. Our firm has been involved in the export of raw silk, and we are confident in our experience in inspecting quality. All Chinese silk sold by our firm to American factories has satisfied our clients. Moreover, our firm consistently holds a leading position in the quantity of raw silk exported, which is a clear demonstration. The alleged claim for damages from silk mills is entirely unfounded. American manufacturers are extremely satisfied with the raw silk sold by our firm and would never claim damages from us. Therefore, there is no basis for our firm to claim damages from silk mills. Although the name "Landis & Company" in the newspaper differs from our firm's name by one character, the pronunciation is similar, and among American raw silk exporters, only our firm, Landis & Company, exists, and there is no such firm as "Landis & Company." It is clear that the article refers to our firm. As this matter concerns our reputation, we dare not remain silent. We are therefore sending this special letter for correction.

Sincerely,

Landis & Company

February 11, 1936

Letter from Attorney Arnhold 109

A news item in your newspaper on the 6th of this month damaged the reputation of my client, Landis & Company, an American merchant. The facts stated in the article regarding the company are completely unfounded. Please correct it immediately.

To the Editor, Shen Bao

February 8

Arnhold Law Offices

170 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, Hamilton Building

Local News

French Concession Ratepayers' Association Firmly Opposes Telephone Metered Billing 110

Sends Letter to French Municipal Council Requesting Rejection, Enumerating Points of Unreasonableness, Repeatedly Refuting Their Justification

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession of this city believes that the Shanghai Telephone Company's proposed change in billing system, at a time of extreme global economic panic, is highly unreasonable. Yesterday, they listed reasons in a letter to the French Municipal Council, requesting its adoption and rejection. The original text is as follows: "To the Editor, We understand that the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Telephone Company will conduct a final review of the proposed change in the billing system this month on the 15th for decision. This matter concerns the economic well-being of citizens and could affect the prosperity of the entire commercial sector, which has already attracted the attention of all citizens. The company's newly proposed metered billing regulations are largely based on past statistics, effectively raising prices in disguise. This kind of

trickery has been firmly opposed by telephone subscribers. We believe that your council will accommodate public opinion, conduct a thorough investigation of this issue, and reject it. We now list the points of unreasonableness in the company's proposed change in rates below for your council's consideration. Telephones are a public utility. In most Western countries, they are state-owned, purely for the purpose of benefiting the people, and cannot be compared to other commercial enterprises that are solely for profit. Now, the Shanghai Telephone Company, with revenue from its existing 36,000 lines, is unable to obtain an annual interest rate of one percent. It insists on

raising revenue for 40,000 lines, unfairly distributing the burden of 40,000 lines onto the 36,000 existing subscribers. Therefore, it must raise prices and change the billing system to achieve its objective. If the number of existing 36,000 subscribers decreases in the future, it will allow the remaining subscribers to bear the increased burden. Its fundamental concept of maintaining a one percent interest rate is entirely flawed. This is the first point of unreasonableness. Since taking over the operation in 1928, the company has consistently generated surpluses of hundreds of thousands or more annually, mainly due to the expansion of capital, which has prevented the distribution of due interest. However, in the company's business performance, there has been no deficit. If the company can expand gradually according to actual conditions, it is not difficult to achieve the desired one percent interest rate. Yet, the company intends to recoup the cost of a 200,000-line telephone system from tens of thousands of subscribers. This measure, which is contrary to economic principles, amounts to

unjustly extracting wealth from telephone subscribers to complete its plan. This is the second point of unreasonableness. It is difficult to determine what price the company has set as appropriate. This kind of statistical data should take into account the prosperity and decline of various industries throughout the city to be accurate. Currently, the entire world is experiencing extreme economic panic, and all industries are declining. The company's desire to

prosper alone amidst universal decline is, in fact, impossible. Social economies are interconnected, and no enterprise can exist in isolation. This change in billing methods by the company is suitable for planning for the future but not for implementation in today's depressed market. The company's closed-door approach, without observing social conditions, is the third point of unreasonableness. According to the company's new billing regulations, residential telephones will be charged six yuan and five jiao per month, limited to 100 calls, and commercial telephones will be charged ten yuan per month, limited to 150 calls. Beyond these limits, each additional call will be charged three cents. On the surface, this seems fair. Metered billing is a common practice in various countries, but the strictness of the restrictions and

the severity of the charges are unparalleled elsewhere. The cost of 100 calls for a residential telephone is six yuan and five jiao, so the cost per call is six and a half cents. The cost of 150 calls for a commercial telephone is ten yuan, so the cost per call is slightly more than six and a third cents. There is no basis for determining this price. This kind of

skimming technique can hardly convince people and is something that telephone subscribers cannot help but resist. In our humble opinion, metered billing for telephones may be feasible, but since the charge for each call beyond the limit is three cents, what justification is there for charging more than six cents per call within the limit? If the basic price is six yuan and five jiao or ten yuan, then the limit for residential telephones should be 200 calls or more, and the limit for commercial telephones should be 300 calls or more. If the company insists on using 100 and 150 calls as the basic quantity, then the prices should be three yuan and four yuan and five jiao, otherwise we cannot consider this equitable. Moreover, according to Article 3, Paragraph 3 of the contract between the company and telephone subscribers, 'Future increases or decreases in telephone rates may be implemented with the approval of the Municipal Council at any time.' A detailed translation of the text reveals that both parties have the right to request changes, but neither party can make unilateral demands. We are sending this letter in the hope that your council will reject the company's request, thereby eliminating the brewing conflict and bringing great satisfaction. To the French Municipal Council."

First Special District Citizens' Association Warns Telephone Company to Postpone Implementation of New Regulations 111

To Await Market Recovery and Avoid Provoking Incidents

The First Special District Citizens' Association of this city yesterday sent a letter to the telephone company in the concession, warning them about the impending implementation of the metered billing system for telephones starting March 1. They urged the company to consider the difficulty of defying public outrage and requested a postponement of the implementation. The original text is as follows: "To the Editor, Although your company's decision on the metered billing system has been researched by experts from various countries, the scope of research granted to these experts by the Municipal Council was too narrow. Furthermore, the Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association's request to expand the scope of research was not adopted, and sufficient consideration was not given to the public will and the actual situation in the market. After repeated study by this association, we believe that the current economic depression is pervasive, and the general public is tightening their belts and scrimping and saving to struggle with this bleak market situation. Your company's desire to drain the pond to catch all the fish, forcing the situation to a dead end, is unwise and undesirable. It should be understood that it is difficult to defy public outrage and achieve selfish desires. We are sending this sincere letter in the hope that you will recognize the meaning of weathering the storm together, postpone the implementation of the new regulations, and await the recovery of the market to avoid provoking incidents."

New U.S. Consul General to Shanghai, Gauss, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 112

Expresses Great Pleasure at Returning to Familiar Ground, Scheduled to Take Office at Consulate Today

The newly appointed U.S. Consul General to Shanghai, Mr. Gauss, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM aboard the Dollar Steamship Company's President Hoover. Acting U.S. Consul General Davis, Counselor Baker, and Acheson of the U.S. Embassy in China were present at the pier to welcome him. Mr. Gauss exchanged brief pleasantries with the welcomers on the ship before crossing the river by small launch. He disembarked at the Custom House Wharf at 4:30 PM. Others present to welcome him there included Administrative Consul Stanton of the U.S. Consulate and President Pan Lai and Secretary Herst of the American Chamber of Commerce. Mr. Gauss is staying at the Metropole Hotel on Jiangxi Road. His family did not accompany him.

Takes Office Today

Mr. Gauss told a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency on the ship that he had previously traveled in China for many years. He was very pleased to be appointed as Consul General to Shanghai, as it was a return to familiar ground. He would follow the example of his predecessors in all consular matters. Plans for the construction of a new consulate building may not be realized for several months. It is reported that he is scheduled to take office at the consulate today (the 12th). Mr. Gauss is 49 years old, born in Washington in 1887. He joined the State Department in 1904. He first came to China on June 7, 1907, as Vice Consul to Shanghai. He returned to the U.S. two years later. In 1912, he came to Shanghai again as Vice Consul. In 1915, he was reassigned as Deputy Consul. In 1916, he was transferred to Tianjin and Xiamen as Consul. In 1919, he was transferred to Jinan. In 1923, he was transferred to Shenyang. In 1924, he returned to Tianjin. He also served as Acting Consul General to Shanghai when the former U.S. Consul General, Mr. Cunningham, took leave in August 1926. He returned to Tianjin in 1927 and returned to the U.S. in 1931, where he worked in the State Department. In 1933, he came to China for the third time as Counselor of the U.S. Legation in China. He was transferred to the U.S. Embassy in France as Counselor and Consul General in Paris on February 27 of last year. After the former U.S. Consul General to Shanghai, Mr. Cunningham, returned to the U.S. at the end of last year, he was ordered to be transferred from Paris to Shanghai. He returned to the U.S. from Paris at the beginning of this year for instructions and then came to China. This is his fourth visit. His rank is that of a first-class consul general.

Davis Transferred to New Post

The current acting U.S. Consul General to Shanghai, Mr. Davis, has been ordered to be transferred to Singapore as Consul General. Mr. Davis told a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday that he is scheduled to take office in Singapore on April 1 and plans to leave Shanghai by the end of March to visit Nanjing, Peiping, and Tianjin before returning to Shanghai to await his ship. It is also reported that Mr. Cole, who has been transferred from Hong Kong to Shanghai as Consul, and Mr. Ander, who has been transferred from Calcutta, India, to Shanghai, will arrive in Shanghai successively by the end of this month to take up their new posts.

British Ambassador Returns Home 113

Departs Shanghai on April 14 for Six-Month Leave, Meets with Ross Yesterday Morning, Returns to Nanjing This Friday

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, British Ambassador to China Sir Frederick Leith-Ross arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing at 10:50 PM the night before. He met with Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, the British economic expert to China, at the Cathay Hotel yesterday morning at approximately 9:00 AM to discuss various matters. A Xin Sheng News Agency reporter visited Mr. Graham, the private secretary to Ambassador Leith-Ross, yesterday morning. According to Mr. Graham, the ambassador will return to England. The departure date has been set for April 14. He, his wife, and his daughter will depart from Shanghai on the P&O liner Naldera. The leave will last for six months, and he will return to China before the end of this year. The ambassador's trip is a routine leave and does not involve any special mission. It is customary for British diplomats to return to England for a leave every two years. This trip to Shanghai is also in the nature of a sightseeing visit. He is scheduled to stay for three days and will return to Nanjing this Friday, possibly returning to Shanghai when it is time to board the ship. However, according to informed sources in Chinese and foreign diplomatic circles, Sir Frederick Leith-Ross's return to England is actually on an important mission related to Britain's attitude towards the Far East issue. Sir Frederick Leith-Ross's return to England is partly to report on various situations in China and partly to seek instructions from his national authorities.

Three British Far East Air Force Flying Boats to Arrive in Shanghai on the 20th 114

Stay in Shanghai for Two Days, Depart for Japan on the 23rd

The British Far East Air Force has specifically dispatched three flying boats from No. 205 Squadron stationed in Singapore for a goodwill tour between China and Japan (not exclusively to Japan). Led by Air Officer Commanding, Singapore, Smith, they departed from Singapore the day before yesterday. According to Mr. Willock, the aviation attaché of the British Embassy in China, the complete itinerary of the three boats is as follows: 10th day, Singapore to Kuching; 11th day, Kuching to Kudat; 12th day, Kudat to Manila; 13th and 14th days, in Manila; 15th day, Manila to Hong Kong; 16th and 17th days, in Hong Kong; 18th day, Hong Kong to Amoy; 19th day, in Amoy; 20th day, Amoy to Shanghai; 21st and 22nd days, stay in Shanghai; 23rd day, fly from Shanghai to Kagoshima, Japan; 24th day, in Kagoshima; 25th day, Kagoshima to Kasumigaura. For the return journey, they will fly from Kasumigaura to Kagoshima on the first day of the following month; 2nd day, in Kagoshima; 3rd day, fly from Kagoshima to Shanghai; 4th and 5th days, stay in Shanghai again; 6th day, fly from Shanghai to Hong Kong; 7th and 8th days, in Hong Kong; 9th day, fly from Hong Kong to Cam Ranh Bay; 10th day, fly from Cam Ranh Bay back to Singapore. British officials and residents in this city have been ordered by the British Ambassador to China not to make a big welcome when the three boats arrive in Shanghai in memory of the late King George VI.

According to a Reuters report from this city on the 11th, three flying boats of the British Air Force's No. 205 Squadron departed from Singapore yesterday, intending to make a 7,000-mile flight to and from Tokyo. According to official news received today, the three flying boats have suspended their flight after arriving at Kuching, the first stop in Sarawak, northern Borneo, due to bad weather. It is likely that they will depart from Kuching tomorrow for Manila and then proceed to Japan via Hong Kong, Amoy, and Shanghai.

The Mint Is Expediting the Production of New Coins 116

Announcements Are Being Made to Use Them as Much as Possible

The new subsidiary coins cast by the Central Mint under the order of the Ministry of Finance went into circulation on the 10th of this month. The general public is happy to exchange them due to their attractive appearance, novelty, and ease of calculation. In recent days, those exchanging coins at the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications have been very crowded. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications have already exhausted their supply yesterday. The Central Mint is now rushing to produce more coins to meet the demand. The details are as follows:

Railway Bureau Announces the Use of New Coins at All Stations

The accounting offices of the Jinghu Railway, the Huhu Railway, and the Huhangyong Railway jointly announced yesterday that the Central Bank has issued new copper half-cent and one-cent coins and nickel five-cent, ten-cent, and twenty-cent coins starting from the 10th of this month. All stations on the railway are required to accept these coins for payment of all kinds of freight charges and passenger ticket balances. The existing copper and silver subsidiary coins must still be accepted until the government announces their discontinuation. However, all stations on the railway should use only new coins or large foreign currency certificates for the balance of passenger tickets and freight charges and should not use old subsidiary coins or copper coins for change. The new subsidiary coins needed by each station on the 10th of this month will first be sent by this office after carefully considering the quantity needed by each station as a special advance to be used for this purpose. If the new subsidiary coins are still insufficient, each stationmaster should exchange national currency certificates for them at the Bank of Communications or this office to benefit the merchants.

Tobacco and Exchange Industry Slightly Charges a Handling Fee

A person in charge of the local tobacco and exchange industry association told a reporter from the Da Gong News Agency yesterday that the new subsidiary coins began to circulate on the market only one day ago. Residents in the urban area are using legal tender to exchange them at the association's stores. All tobacco and exchange stores in the northern and southern districts belonging to the association are complying with the orders of the Ministry of Finance and are successively receiving large quantities of new subsidiary coins from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications to meet market needs. However, to maintain the business interests of the industry, a slight handling fee is still charged to those who come to exchange them. The handling fee signs in each tobacco and exchange store are not yet uniform, but there are general restrictions to prevent the fee from being too high. The exchange rate for old subsidiary coins remains the same as before.

Chinese Industrial Association, etc. Hosted a Banquet for the Qingdao Observation Group Yesterday 119

Over twenty members of the group, including all the team members and Guo Shun, etc., attended. The group is scheduled to visit the China Alcohol Factory today.

Following their arrival in Shanghai, the Qingdao Industrial Safety and Hygiene Observation Group has been quite busy visiting various factories in recent days. Yesterday afternoon, they were also guests of honor at a banquet hosted by the China General Industries Federation and the Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factories Joint Association. In the afternoon, they visited the China Bookstore. The details of each event are recorded below.

Yesterday Afternoon's Banquet

At 12:00 noon yesterday, the China General Industries Federation and the Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factories Joint Association specially hosted a banquet for the Qingdao Industrial Safety and Hygiene Observation Group at the China General Industries Federation's clubhouse on Hankou Road. Those in attendance included the group's leader Wang Shouze, members Sun Siqing, Chen Yuhan, Xu Biao, Yao Junhe, Zhou Zixi, Chen Yaoyao, Guan Xibin, Li Shikui, as well as the two associations' committee members Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Cai Shengbai, Zhu Gengtao, Wang Qiyu, Qian Chengxu, Wang Zhisheng, Wu YunChu, Lu Zhixue, Cheng Shouzhong, and over twenty others. Lu Zhixue was publicly elected chairman and delivered a welcoming speech, followed by a response from group leader Wang Shouze. The hosts and guests enjoyed themselves until around 2:00 PM, when the banquet concluded.

Chairman's Speech

Lu Zhixue began by delivering a welcoming speech, stating roughly, "Gentlemen, today, both of our organizations jointly welcome the Qingdao Industrial Safety and Hygiene Observation Group. We are deeply honored by your presence. In recent years, Chinese industry has shown rapid progress. However, the faster the progress, the more difficult it is to manage capital. Factory management cannot be effective without scientific methods. In this regard, there are two urgent issues that need attention: Management organization and industrial safety. Regarding the latter, after several studies, we have realized that if personnel issues are not resolved, industrial management cannot be perfected, and if mechanical equipment is not safe, workers will always be at risk. The result will undoubtedly affect production. Recently, the Ministry of Industry, feeling the need to promote industrial safety in Chinese factories, held an industrial safety and hygiene exhibition in the capital some time ago. This allowed general factories across the country, especially those interested in such equipment and enthusiastically promoting it, to visit and observe. In addition to their observation, they were able to promote improvements in their own businesses. The intention was excellent. The Qingdao industrial factories, under the guidance of Mayor Shen, organized an observation group, spared no effort to travel to the capital to study, and now, based on their observations, they are visiting factories in Shanghai for further investigation. Their spirit and perseverance are admirable. We hope that your esteemed group will generously share your findings as a reference for our colleagues. Today, we have prepared a simple banquet to wish you good health."

Group Leader's Response

Next, group leader Wang Shouze delivered a response, stating roughly, "Brothers, I am entrusted by Qingdao Mayor Shen to organize an industrial safety observation group to travel to various locations along the Beijing-Shanghai railway line for investigation, as a reference for Qingdao's industry. We have visited major factories in the capital, Wuxi, Suzhou, and other places, and the impressions we gained were excellent, especially from the industrial safety and hygiene exhibition organized by the Ministry of Industry. Now, we have come to Shanghai, and we are very grateful to your association for hosting a banquet and introducing us to factories for visits. However, our abilities are limited. We hope that all the gentlemen present will provide guidance so that Qingdao's industry can thrive."

Today's Schedule

All members of the group visited the Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory at 9:00 AM yesterday. Accompanied by the factory staff, they visited the weaving workshop and dyeing workshop to observe various safety equipment. They then went to the Tianli Gas Factory. After being led on a tour by factory manager Wu YunChu, it was noon. They immediately went to the China General Industries Federation on Hankou Road for a banquet. After the banquet ended around 2:00 PM, they went to the China Bookstore on Jing'an Temple Road to observe the factory's entire equipment and inquire about management and labor welfare matters in detail. They finished their work around 6:00 PM and returned to their residence to rest. They are scheduled to visit the Zhanghua Wool Weaving Factory and the Huafeng Enamel Factory this morning, and the China Alcohol Factory this afternoon.

The Sugar Industry Held an Emergency Meeting Yesterday 121

Offering a reward of 500 yuan to prevent smuggling.

Since the Ministry of Finance revised the sugar tax regulations the year before last, tax evasion and smuggling have emerged endlessly. This trend is particularly rampant in South and North China. Last winter, smuggling also occurred in Hankou, Xuzhou, Bengbu, and other places. Recently, there were plans to smuggle sugar into Shanghai. Upon hearing this, the Shanghai Sugar Trade Association believed that it would harm national taxes above and sugar merchants below. Therefore, they convened an emergency meeting yesterday to find ways to prevent it. Three measures were decided on the spot: 1. Petition the Ministry of Finance to strictly crack down on smuggling. 2. Warn all members not to buy sugar of unknown origin. 3. Issue a notice offering a reward of 500 yuan for confidential reports.
